I have a fun theory that will probably be debunked before the pilot even airs: Uzi is either A: Actually a Murder Drone, which would explain her  brave though violent behavior while the other worker drones seem to be somewhat cowardly and peaceful. B: has a malfunction in her software that causes her behavior that surfaced some time before humanity killed itself, the "Parent Company" could have attempted to fix it but was unable to before they died, which would explain her animosity toward them. Or C: the Parent Company purposely built her the way she is because they were already planning on creating the murder drones, meaning that she is a early Prototype. I don't know a lot about technology, but electronic-based products tend to go through multiple versions before being sold to the public, so the current design of the Murder Drones could be the result of wanting to make them more intimidating.  Something else I noticed: alot of the worker drones seem to be male, while a lot of the murder drones (that I can see) seem to be female.   Also, a major plot point could be how neither Uzi nor N entirely fit in alongside their fellows. From the trailer, Uzi seems to be the only one among the worker drones who is actually prepared to fight the Murder Drones despite them possessing superior abilities while N seems to be the only Murder Drone who possesses any feelings besides bloodlust.If the Murder Drones are supposed to be heartless killers while Worker Drones are laborers, neither of them entirely fit the mold.   A couple of things could easily debunk this theory:   1: if Uzi is a murder drone, she doesn't possess the same colors. (MDs all seem to have silver hair , scissor fingers, yellow eyes/lights, and syringe like scorpion looking tails. Uzi has Purple hair and Eyes, No scissor fingers, and has no tail)  2: Aside from the beginning of the trailer,  Uzi shows no visible signs of malfunction or damage. N has a single red light on his head and his face displays the word "error"in his first appearance, while Uzi doesn't show a red light and the ERROR appeared in her normal color.  3: AI in sci fi literature is often depicted to develop its own personality over time, which seems to be the case with these drones. So Uzis behavior could simply  by sheer coincidence become more violent over time normally.  4: it's just a cartoon and I'm looking into it too much for no reason.  I hope you enjoyed my theory!
